{"parentUuid":"e6fe267e-ad2c-40c5-bc9c-15e6ba6346c4","isSidechain":true,"agentId":"ad80c14b97e58622b","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"call_0a3aabc2110f45d7ab25f55a","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t#!/bin/bash\n2\t\n3\t# =============================================================================\n4\t# SuperMac - Finder Module\n5\t# =============================================================================\n6\t# File visibility and Finder management commands\n7\t# \n8\t# Commands:\n9\t#   restart       - Restart Finder application\n10\t#   show-hidden   - Show hidden files\n11\t#   hide-hidden   - Hide hidden files  \n12\t#   toggle-hidden - Toggle hidden file visibility\n13\t#\n14\t# Built by CosmoLabs - https://cosmolabs.org\n15\t# =============================================================================\n16\t\n17\t# =============================================================================\n18\t# Finder Module Commands\n19\t# =============================================================================\n20\t\n21\tfinder_restart() {\n22\t    print_info \"Restarting Finder...\"\n23\t    \n24\t    if ! pgrep -f \"Finder\" >/dev/null 2>&1; then\n25\t        print_warning \"Finder doesn't appear to be running. Starting it...\"\n26\t        open -a Finder\n27\t        print_success \"Finder started successfully!\"\n28\t        return 0\n29\t    fi\n30\t    \n31\t    if killall Finder 2>/dev/null; then\n32\t        sleep 1\n33\t        \n34\t        # Wait for Finder to restart\n35\t        local timeout=5\n36\t        local count=0\n37\t        while ! pgrep -f \"Finder\" >/dev/null 2>&1 && [[ $count -lt $timeout ]]; do\n38\t            sleep 1\n39\t            ((count++))\n40\t        done\n41\t        \n42\t        if pgrep -f \"Finder\" >/dev/null 2>&1; then\n43\t            print_success \"Finder restarted successfully!\"\n44\t            print_info \"💡 Tip: This often fixes unresponsive Finder windows\"\n45\t        else\n46\t            print_warning \"Finder may not have restarted properly. Opening manually...\"\n47\t            open -a Finder\n48\t            print_success \"Finder opened manually\"\n49\t        fi\n50\t    else\n51\t        print_error \"Failed to restart Finder\"\n52\t        print_info \"You may need to restart Finder manually from Activity Monitor\"\n53\t        return 1\n54\t    fi\n55\t}\n56\t\n57\t# Get current hidden files state\n58\tfinder_get_hidden_state() {\n59\t    local current_state\n60\t    current_state=$(defaults read com.apple.finder AppleShowAllFiles 2>/dev/null || echo \"FALSE\")\n61\t    \n62\t    case \"$(to_upper \"$current_state\")\" in\n63\t        \"TRUE\"|\"1\"|\"YES\")\n64\t            echo \"visible\"\n65\t            ;;\n66\t        *)\n67\t            echo \"hidden\"\n68\t            ;;\n69\t    esac\n70\t}\n71\t\n72\tfinder_show_hidden() {\n73\t    local current_state\n74\t    current_state=$(finder_get_hidden_state)\n75\t    \n76\t    if [[ \"$current_state\" == \"visible\" ]]; then\n77\t        print_info \"Hidden files are already visible\"\n78\t        return 0\n79\t    fi\n80\t    \n81\t    print_info \"Making hidden files visible...\"\n82\t    defaults write com.apple.finder AppleShowAllFiles TRUE\n83\t    \n84\t    if killall Finder 2>/dev/null; then\n85\t        sleep 1\n86\t        print_success \"Hidden files are now visible!\"\n87\t        print_info \"💡 You can now see files like .gitignore, .env, .DS_Store\"\n88\t        print_info \"💡 Use 'mac finder hide-hidden' to hide them again\"\n89\t    else\n90\t        print_error \"Failed to restart Finder\"\n91\t        print_info \"Changes may not take effect until Finder is restarted\"\n92\t        return 1\n93\t    fi\n94\t}\n95\t\n96\tfinder_hide_hidden() {\n97\t    local current_state\n98\t    current_state=$(finder_get_hidden_state)\n99\t    \n100\t    if [[ \"$current_state\" == \"hidden\" ]]; then\n101\t        print_info \"Hidden files are already hidden\"\n102\t        return 0\n103\t    fi\n104\t    \n105\t    print_info \"Hiding hidden files...\"\n106\t    defaults write com.apple.finder AppleShowAllFiles FALSE\n107\t    \n108\t    if killall Finder 2>/dev/null; then\n109\t        sleep 1\n110\t        print_success \"Hidden files are now hidden!\"\n111\t        print_info \"💡 Clean view restored - system files are tucked away\"\n112\t        print_info \"💡 Use 'mac finder show-hidden' to show them again\"\n113\t    else\n114\t        print_error \"Failed to restart Finder\"\n115\t        print_info \"Changes may not take effect until Finder is restarted\"\n116\t        return 1\n117\t    fi\n118\t}\n119\t\n120\tfinder_toggle_hidden() {\n121\t    local current_state\n122\t    current_state=$(finder_get_hidden_state)\n123\t    \n124\t    print_info \"Current state: Hidden files are $current_state\"\n125\t    \n126\t    if [[ \"$current_state\" == \"visible\" ]]; then\n127\t        defaults write com.apple.finder AppleShowAllFiles FALSE\n128\t        print_info \"Setting hidden files to HIDDEN\"\n129\t    else\n130\t        defaults write com.apple.finder AppleShowAllFiles TRUE\n131\t        print_info \"Setting hidden files to VISIBLE\"\n132\t    fi\n133\t    \n134\t    print_info \"Applying changes...\"\n135\t    if killall Finder 2>/dev/null; then\n136\t        sleep 1\n137\t        local new_state\n138\t        new_state=$(finder_get_hidden_state)\n139\t        print_success \"Hidden files are now $new_state!\"\n140\t        \n141\t        if [[ \"$new_state\" == \"visible\" ]]; then\n142\t            print_info \"💡 You can now see system files and hidden folders\"\n143\t        else\n144\t            print_info \"💡 System files are now hidden for a cleaner view\"\n145\t        fi\n146\t    else\n147\t        print_error \"Failed to restart Finder\"\n148\t        return 1\n149\t    fi\n150\t}\n151\t\n152\tfinder_reveal() {\n153\t    local target=\"$1\"\n154\t    \n155\t    if [[ -z \"$target\" ]]; then\n156\t        print_error \"Path required\"\n157\t        print_info \"Usage: mac finder reveal <path>\"\n158\t        return 1\n159\t    fi\n160\t    \n161\t    if [[ ! -e \"$target\" ]]; then\n162\t        print_error \"Path does not exist: $target\"\n163\t        return 1\n164\t    fi\n165\t    \n166\t    print_info \"Revealing '$target' in Finder...\"\n167\t    open -R \"$target\"\n168\t    print_success \"Path revealed in Finder!\"\n169\t}\n170\t\n171\tfinder_status() {\n172\t    print_header \"📁 Finder Status\"\n173\t    echo \"\"\n174\t    \n175\t    # Check if Finder is running\n176\t    if pgrep -f \"Finder\" >/dev/null 2>&1; then\n177\t        print_success \"Finder is running\"\n178\t    else\n179\t        print_warning \"Finder is not running\"\n180\t    fi\n181\t    \n182\t    # Check hidden files state\n183\t    local hidden_state\n184\t    hidden_state=$(finder_get_hidden_state)\n185\t    echo \"  Hidden files: $(print_command \"$hidden_state\")\"\n186\t    \n187\t    # Check Finder preferences\n188\t    local show_extensions\n189\t    show_extensions=$(defaults read NSGlobalDomain AppleShowAllExtensions 2>/dev/null || echo \"0\")\n190\t    if [[ \"$show_extensions\" == \"1\" ]]; then\n191\t        echo \"  File extensions: $(print_command \"visible\")\"\n192\t    else\n193\t        echo \"  File extensions: $(print_dim \"hidden\")\"\n194\t    fi\n195\t    \n196\t    # Show default view style\n197\t    local view_style\n198\t    view_style=$(defaults read com.apple.finder FXPreferredViewStyle 2>/dev/null || echo \"icnv\")\n199\t    case \"$view_style\" in\n200\t        \"icnv\") echo \"  Default view: $(print_command \"Icon View\")\" ;;\n201\t        \"Nlsv\") echo \"  Default view: $(print_command \"List View\")\" ;;\n202\t        \"clmv\") echo \"  Default view: $(print_command \"Column View\")\" ;;\n203\t        \"Flwv\") echo \"  Default view: $(print_command \"Gallery View\")\" ;;\n204\t        *) echo \"  Default view: $(print_dim \"Unknown\")\" ;;\n205\t    esac\n206\t}\n207\t\n208\t# =============================================================================\n209\t# Module Help System\n210\t# =============================================================================\n211\t\n212\tfinder_help() {\n213\t    print_category_header \"finder\" \"📁\" 65\n214\t    \n215\t    printf \"${PURPLE}│${NC}  %-20s %-35s ${PURPLE}│${NC}\\n\" \"restart\" \"Restart Finder application\"\n216\t    printf \"${PURPLE}│${NC}  %-20s %-35s ${PURPLE}│${NC}\\n\" \"show-hidden\" \"Show hidden files and folders\"\n217\t    printf \"${PURPLE}│${NC}  %-20s %-35s ${PURPLE}│${NC}\\n\" \"hide-hidden\" \"Hide hidden files and folders\"\n218\t    printf \"${PURPLE}│${NC}  %-20s %-35s ${PURPLE}│${NC}\\n\" \"toggle-hidden\" \"Toggle hidden file visibility\"\n219\t    printf \"${PURPLE}│${NC}  %-20s %-35s ${PURPLE}│${NC}\\n\" \"reveal <path>\" \"Reveal file/folder in Finder\"\n220\t    printf \"${PURPLE}│${NC}  %-20s %-35s ${PURPLE}│${NC}\\n\" \"status\" \"Show Finder status and settings\"\n221\t    \n222\t    print_category_footer 65\n223\t    echo \"\"\n224\t    \n225\t    print_header \"Examples:\"\n226\t    echo \"  mac finder restart              # Fix unresponsive Finder\"\n227\t    echo \"  mac finder toggle-hidden        # Quick toggle hidden files\"\n228\t    echo \"  mac finder reveal ~/.ssh        # Show .ssh folder in Finder\"\n229\t    echo \"  mac finder status               # Check current settings\"\n230\t    echo \"\"\n231\t    \n232\t    print_header \"Shortcuts:\"\n233\t    echo \"  mac restart-finder              # Global shortcut for restart\"\n234\t    echo \"\"\n235\t    \n236\t    print_header \"Tips:\"\n237\t    echo \"  • Hidden files include system files like .DS_Store, .gitignore\"\n238\t    echo \"  • Showing hidden files is useful for development work\"\n239\t    echo \"  • Restart Finder if windows become unresponsive\"\n240\t    echo \"  • Use reveal to quickly navigate to specific files\"\n241\t    echo \"\"\n242\t}\n243\t\n244\t# Search function for this module\n245\tfinder_search() {\n246\t    local search_term=\"$1\"\n247\t    local results=\"\"\n248\t    \n249\t    # Search through command names and descriptions\n250\t    if [[ \"restart\" == *\"$search_term\"* ]] || [[ \"finder\" == *\"$search_term\"* ]]; then\n251\t        results+=\"  mac finder restart              Restart Finder application\\n\"\n252\t    fi\n253\t    \n254\t    if [[ \"hidden\" == *\"$search_term\"* ]] || [[ \"show\" == *\"$search_term\"* ]] || [[ \"hide\" == *\"$search_term\"* ]]; then\n255\t        results+=\"  mac finder show-hidden          Show hidden files\\n\"\n256\t        results+=\"  mac finder hide-hidden          Hide hidden files\\n\"\n257\t        results+=\"  mac finder toggle-hidden        Toggle hidden files\\n\"\n258\t    fi\n259\t    \n260\t    if [[ \"reveal\" == *\"$search_term\"* ]] || [[ \"open\" == *\"$search_term\"* ]]; then\n261\t        results+=\"  mac finder reveal <path>        Reveal in Finder\\n\"\n262\t    fi\n263\t    \n264\t    if [[ \"status\" == *\"$search_term\"* ]] || [[ \"info\" == *\"$search_term\"* ]]; then\n265\t        results+=\"  mac finder status               Show Finder status\\n\"\n266\t    fi\n267\t    \n268\t    if [[ -n \"$results\" ]]; then\n269\t        echo -e \"$results\"\n270\t    fi\n271\t}\n272\t\n273\t# =============================================================================\n274\t# Module Dispatcher\n275\t# =============================================================================\n276\t\n277\tfinder_dispatch() {\n278\t    local action=\"$1\"\n279\t    shift  # Remove action from arguments\n280\t    \n281\t    case \"$action\" in\n282\t        \"restart\")\n283\t            finder_restart\n284\t            ;;\n285\t        \"show-hidden\")\n286\t            finder_show_hidden\n287\t            ;;\n288\t        \"hide-hidden\")\n289\t            finder_hide_hidden\n290\t            ;;\n291\t        \"toggle-hidden\")\n292\t            finder_toggle_hidden\n293\t            ;;\n294\t        \"reveal\")\n295\t            finder_reveal \"$@\"\n296\t            ;;\n297\t        \"status\")\n298\t            finder_status\n299\t \n90\t    if [[ -z \"$interface\" ]]; then\n91\t        print_error \"WiFi interface not found\"\n92\t        return 1\n93\t    fi\n94\t    \n95\t    local current_state\n96\t \n122\t    print_info \"Current WiFi state: $current_state\"\n123\t    \n124\t    case \"$current_state\" in\n125\t        \"On\")\n126\t            wifi_off\n127\t            ;;\n128\t \n146\t    if [[ -z \"$interface\" ]]; then\n147\t        return 1\n148\t    fi\n149\t    \n150\t    local network\n151\t    network=$(networksetup -getairportnetwork \"$interface\" 2>/dev/null | sed \n466\t    case \"$action\" in\n467\t        \"on\"|\"enable\")\n468\t            wifi_on\n469\t            ;;\n470\t        \"off\"|\"disable\")\n471\t            wifi_off\n472\t            ;;\n473\t    current_size=$(dock_get_size)\n187\t    \n188\t    if [[ \"$current_size\" == \"$size\" ]]; then\n189\t        print_info \"Dock size is already set to $size\"\n190\t        return 0\n191\t =============================================================================\n214\t# Dock Magnification Functions\n215\t# =============================================================================\n106\t# System Cleanup Functions\n107\t# =============================================================================\n108\t\n109\tsystem_cleanup() {\n110\t    print_header \"🧹 System Cleanup\"\n111\t    echo \"\"\n112\t    \n113\t   \n149\t    # Trash\n150\t    print_info \"Emptying trash...\"\n151\t    osascript -e 'tell application \"Finder\" to empty trash' 2>/dev/null || true\n152\t    print_success \"Trash emptied\"\n153\t required)...\"\n157\t        sudo find /var/log -name \"*.log\" -mtime +7 -delete 2>/dev/null || true\n158\t        sudo find /private/var/log -name \"*.log\" -mtime +7 -delete 2>/dev/null || true\n159\t        print_success \"System logs cleaned\"\n160\t    else\n161\t        print_info \"Skipping system logs (no admin privileges)\"\n162\t    fi\n163\t    \n164\t    # Browser caches (Safari)\n165\t    if [[ -d \"$HOME/Library/Caches/com.apple.Safari\" ]]; then\n166\t        print_info \"Cleaning Safari cache...\"\n167\t        rm -rf \"$HOME/Library/Caches/com.apple.Safari\"/* 2>/dev/null || true\n168\t        print_success \"Safari cache cleaned\"\n169\t    fi\n170\t    \n171\t    # Temporary files\n172\t    print_info \"Cleaning temporary files...\"\n173\t    rm -rf /tmp/* 2>/dev/null || true\n174\t    print_success \"Temporary files cleaned\"\n175\t    \n176\t    # Font caches\n177\t    print_info \"Clearing font caches...\"\n178\t    sudo atsutil databases -remove 2>/dev/null || true\n179\t    print_success \"Font caches cleared\"\n180\t    \n181\t    echo \"\"\n182\t    print_success \"System cleanup completed!\"\n183\t    print_info \"💡 Consider restarting applications to free additional memory\"\n184\t    print_info \"💡 Use 'mac system memory' to check current memory usage\"\n185\t}\n186\t\n187\t# =============================================================================\n188\t# Battery Information\n189\t# =============================================================================\n190\t\n191\tsystem_battery() {\n192\t    # Check if this is a laptop\n193\t    if ! system_profiler SPPowerDataType >/dev/null 2>&1; then\n194\t        print_info \"No battery information available (desktop Mac)\"\n195\t        return 0\n196\t    fi\n197\t    \n198\t    print_header \"🔋 Battery Information\"\n199\t    echo \"\"\n200\t    \n201\t    # Get battery info using pmset\n202\t    local battery_info\n203\t    battery_info=$(pmset -g batt 2>/dev/null)\n204\t    \n205\t    if [[ -n \"$battery_info\" ]]; then\n206\t        # Parse battery percentage and status\n207\t        local percentage status time_remaining\n208\t        percentage=$(echo \"$battery_info\" | grep -E \"InternalBattery\" | awk '{print $3}' | sed 's/;//')\n209\t        status=$(echo \"$battery_info\" | grep -E \"InternalBattery\" | awk '{print $4}' | sed 's/;//')\n210\t        time_remaining=$(echo \"$battery_info\" | grep -E \"InternalBattery\" | awk '{for(i=5;i<=NF;i++) printf \"%s \", $i; print \"\"}' | trim)\n211\t        \n212\t        echo \"  Charge: $(print_command \"$percentage\")\"\n213\t        echo \"  Status: $(print_command \"$status\")\"\n214\t        \n215\t        if [[ -n \"$time_remaining\" && \"$time_remaining\" != \"(no estimate)\" ]]; then\n216\t            echo \"  Time remaining: $(print_command \"$time_remaining\")\"\n217\t        fi\n218\t    fi\n219\t    \n220\t    # Battery health information\n221\t    local cycle_count max_capacity\n222\t    cycle_count=$(system_profiler SPPowerDataType 2>/dev/null | grep \"Cycle Count\" | awk -F': ' '{print $2}' | trim)\n223\t    max_capacity=$(system_profiler SPPowerDataType 2>/dev/null | grep \"Maximum Capacity\" | awk -F': ' '{print $2}' | trim)\n224\t    \n225\t    if [[ -n \"$cycle_count\" ]]; then\n226\t        echo \"  Cycle count: $(print_command \"$cycle_count\")\"\n227\t    fi\n228\t    \n229\t    if [[ -n \"$max_capacity\" ]]; then\n230\t        echo \"  Maximum capacity: $(print_command \"$max_capacity\")\"\n231\t        \n232\t        # Health assessment\n233\t        local capacity_num\n234\t        capacity_num=$(echo \"$max_capacity\" | sed 's/%//')\n235\t        if [[ \"$capacity_num\" -gt 80 ]]; then\n236\t            print_success \"Battery health: Good\"\n237\t        elif [[ \"$capacity_num\" -gt 60 ]]; then\n238\t            print_warning \"Battery health: Fair\"\n239\t        else\n240\t            print_warning \"Battery health: Poor (consider replacement)\"\n241\t        fi\n242\t    fi\n243\t    \n244\t    # Power adapter status\n245\t    local adapter_info\n246\t    adapter_info=$(pmset -g ac 2>/dev/null)\n247\t    if [[ \"$adapter_info\" == *\"AC Power\"* ]]; then\n248\t        echo \"  Power adapter: $(print_command \"Connected\")\"\n249\t    else\n250\t        echo \"  Power adapter: $(print_dim \"Not connected\")\"\n251\t    fi\n252\t}\n253\t\n254\t# =============================================================================\n255\t# Memory Information\n256\t# =============================================================================\n257\t\n258\tsystem_memory() {\n259\t    print_header \"💾 Memory Usage\"\n260\t    echo \"\"\n261\t    \n262\t    # Get memory statistics\n263\t    local memory_info\n264\t    memory_info=$(vm_stat)\n265\t    \n266\t    local page_size=4096\n267\t    local pages_free pages_active pages_inactive pages_wired pages_compressed\n268\t    \n269\t    pages_free=$(echo \"$memory_info\" | grep \"Pages free\" | awk '{print $3}' | sed 's/\\.//')\n270\t    pages_active=$(echo \"$memory_info\" | grep \"Pages active\" | awk '{print $3}' | sed 's/\\.//')\n271\t    pages_inactive=$(echo \"$memory_info\" | grep \"Pages inactive\" | awk '{print $3}' | sed 's/\\.//')\n272\t    pages_wired=$(echo \"$memory_info\" | grep \"Pages wired down\" | awk '{print $4}' | sed 's/\\.//')\n273\t    pages_compressed=$(echo \"$memory_info\" | grep \"Pages stored in compressor\" | awk '{print $5}' | sed 's/\\.//' 2>/dev/null || echo \"0\")\n274\t    \n275\t    # Convert to MB\n276\t    local free_mb active_mb inactive_mb wired_mb compressed_mb total_mb used_mb\n277\t    free_mb=$((pages_free * page_size / 1024 / 1024))\n278\t    active_mb=$((pages_active * page_size / 1024 / 1024))\n279\t    inactive_mb=$((pages_inactive * page_size / 1024 / 1024))\n280\t    wired_mb=$((pages_wired * page_size / 1024 / 1024))\n281\t    compressed_mb=$((pages_compressed * page_size / 1024 / 1024))\n282\t    \n283\t    used_mb=$((active_mb + inactive_mb + wired_mb))\n284\t    total_mb=$((free_mb + used_mb))\n285\t    \n286\t    echo \"  Total: $(print_command \"${total_mb} MB\")\"\n287\t    echo \"  Used: $(print_command \"${used_mb} MB\")\"\n288\t    echo \"  Free: $(print_command \"${free_mb} MB\")\"\n289\t    echo \"\"\n290\t    echo \"  Active: $(print_command \"${active_mb} MB\")\"\n291\t    echo \"  Inactive: $(print_command \"${inactive_mb} MB\")\"\n292\t    echo \"  Wired: $(print_command \"${wired_mb} MB\")\"\n293\t    \n294\t    if [[ $compressed_mb -gt 0 ]]; then\n295\t        echo \"  Compressed: $(print_command \"${compressed_mb} MB\")\"\n296\t    fi\n297\t    \n298\t    # Memory pressure\n299\t    local memory_pressure\n300\t    memory_pressure=$(memory_pressure 2>/dev/null | grep \"System-wide memory free percentage\" | awk '{print $NF}' | sed 's/%//')\n301\t    \n302\t    if [[ -n \"$memory_pressure\" ]]; then\n303\t        echo \"\"\n304\t        if [[ \"$memory_pressure\" -gt 20 ]]; then\n305\t            print_success \"Memory pressure: Low ($memory_pressure% free)\"\n306\t        elif [[ \"$memory_pressure\" -gt 10 ]]; then\n307\t            print_warning \"Memory pressure: Medium ($memory_pressure% free)\"\n308\t        else\n309\t            print_warning \"Memory pressure: High ($memory_pressure% free)\"\n310\t            print_info \"💡 Consider closing some applications\"\n311\t        fi\n312\t    fi\n313\t}\n314\t\n315\t# =============================================================================\n316\t# CPU Information\n317\t# =============================================================================\n318\t\n319\tsystem_cpu() {\n320\t    print_header \"⚡ CPU Information\"\n321\t    echo \"\"\n322\t    \n323\t    # CPU model and specs\n324\t    local cpu_name cpu_cores cpu_threads\n325\t    cpu_name=$(sysctl -n machdep.cpu.brand_string 2>/dev/null)\n326\t    cpu_cores=$(sysctl -n hw.physicalcpu 2>/dev/null)\n327\t    cpu_threads=$(sysctl -n hw.logicalcpu 2>/dev/null)\n328\t    \n329\t    if [[ -n \"$cpu_name\" ]]; then\n330\t        echo \"  Processor: $(print_command \"$cpu_name\")\"\n331\t    fi\n332\t    \n333\t    echo \"  Physical cores: $(print_command \"$cpu_cores\")\"\n334\t    echo \"  Logical cores: $(print_command \"$cpu_threads\")\"\n335\t    \n336\t    # CPU usage\n337\t    echo \"\"\n338\t    print_subheader \"Current Usage:\"\n339\t    \n340\t    # Get CPU usage from top\n341\t    local cpu_usage\n342\t    cpu_usage=$(top -l 1 -n 0 | grep \"CPU usage\" | awk '{print $3, $5, $7}')\n343\t    echo \"  $cpu_usage\"\n344\t    \n345\t    # Load average\n346\t    local load_avg\n347\t    load_avg=$(uptime | awk -F'load averages: ' '{print $2}')\n348\t    echo \"  Load average: $(print_command \"$load_avg\")\"\n349\t}\n350\t\n351\t# =============================================================================\n352\t# Disk Usage\n353\t# =============================================================================\n354\t\n355\tsystem_disk_usage() {\n356\t    local target_dir=\"${1:-$HOME}\"\n357\t    \n358\t    if [[ ! -d \"$target_dir\" ]]; then\n359\t        print_error \"Directory not found: $target_dir\"\n360\t        return 1\n361\t    fi\n362\t    \n363\t    print_header \"💿 Disk Usage: $target_dir\"\n364\t $(print_command \"$filesystem\")\"\n369\t        echo \"  Total: $(print_command \"$size\")\"\n370\t        echo \"  Used: $(print_command \"$used\")\"\n371\t        echo \"  Available: $(print_command \"$available\")\"\n372\t        echo \"  Usage: $(print_command \"$capacity\")\"\n373\t    done\n374\t    \n375\t    echo \"\"\n376\t    print_subheader \"Largest directories in $target_dir:\"\n377\t    \n378\t    # Find largest directories\n379\t    du -sh \"$target_dir\"/* 2>/dev/null | sort -hr | head -10 | while read -r size path; do\n380\t        printf \"  %-10s %s\\n\" \"$size\" \"$(basename \"$path\")\"\n381\t    done\n382\t}\n383\t\n384\t# =============================================================================\n385\t# System Processes\n386\t# \n198\t    printf \"\\r${BLUE}[\"\n199\t    printf \"%*s\" \"$filled\" \"\" | tr ' ' \"$fill_char\"\n200\t    printf \"%*s\" \"$empty\" \"\" | tr ' ' \"$empty_char\"\n201\t    printf \"] %d%% \n294\t    echo -e \"${YELLOW}$prompt${NC} \"\n295\t    read -r response\n296\t    \n297\t    case \"$response\" in\n298\t        [yY]|[yY][eE][sS])\n299\t            return 0\n300\t     *)\n308\t            print_warning \"Please answer yes or no.\"\n309\t            confirm \"$1\" \"$default\"\n310\t            ;;\n311\t    esac\n312\t}\n313\t\n314\t# Prompt for input with \n320\t    while true; do\n321\t        echo -e \"${BLUE}$prompt${NC}\"\n322\t        if [[ -n \"$default\" ]]; then\n323\t            echo -e \"${DIM}(default: $default)${NC}\"\n324\t Comprehensive coverage of screenshot settings. take [type] is intuitive. Keyboard shortcut documentation is a useful bonus.\"\n    },\n    \"total_commands\": 85,\n    \"total_with_global_shortcuts\": 91\n  }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n# SuperMac v2.1.0 -- UX & CLI Design Audit\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nSuperMac is a well-structured, thoughtfully designed macOS CLI tool that achieves its stated goal of providing \"professional command-line shortcuts for macOS developers and power users.\" The two-level dispatch architecture (`mac <category> <action>`) is clean and predictable. The help system is thorough, errors are actionable, and the output formatting with Unicode box drawing is visually polished.\n\nThe tool's primary weaknesses are in **accessibility** (no color override mechanism, no ASCII-only mode, emoji-heavy output that is hostile to screen readers) and **discoverability** (the search system is manually curated rather than dynamic, and many useful aliases are undocumented). These are fixable without architectural changes.\n\nScore: **72/100** -- a solid CLI tool that would benefit from attention to accessibility, output mode flexibility, and search quality.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Command Design (78/100)\n\n### What Works\n\nThe `mac <category> <action>` pattern is intuitive and follows the model of successful tools like `git`, `docker`, and `kubectl`. Category names are single common words (finder, wifi, network, system, dev, display, dock, audio, screenshot) that map clearly to their domain. Actions are concise verbs or hyphenated verb phrases.\n\nThe dispatcher architecture is consistent across all 9 modules: every module exports a `${category}_dispatch()` function, and every dispatch function follows the same `case \"$action\" in` pattern. This makes the codebase predictable to extend.\n\nGlobal shortcuts (bin/mac:60-70) are well-chosen for the most common operations. `mac ip`, `mac cleanup`, `mac dark`, `mac light` eliminate the two-level hierarchy for high-frequency commands. The shortcut resolution in `route_command()` cleanly maps back to the category:action pair.\n\nInput validation is thorough: port numbers are checked with `is_number()` (dev.sh:39), brightness is range-checked 0-100 (display.sh:49-51), volume is range-checked 0-100 (audio.sh:51-53), and password length is bounded 4-128 (dev.sh:436-438).\n\n### What Needs Improvement\n\n**Inconsistent toggle naming.** Display uses `toggle-mode`, Finder uses `toggle-hidden`, WiFi uses just `toggle`, and Audio uses `toggle-mute`. The inconsistency means users must memorize each module's convention rather than applying a learned pattern. A standardized `toggle-<noun>` pattern would be more predictable.\n\n**Undocumented aliases.** WiFi accepts `enable`/`disable` as synonyms for `on`/`off` (wifi.sh:467-468). Dock accepts `l`, `b`, `r` for positions (dock.sh:36-41). System accepts `mem` for `memory` (system.sh:513). These are convenient for power users but are invisible to anyone reading the help text. The help output should show these as `(or: enable)` annotations.\n\n**Cryptic shortcut.** The `mac kp` shortcut for `dev:kill-port` is the only shortcut that requires memorization rather than being self-explanatory. Every other shortcut (`ip`, `cleanup`, `dark`, `light`, `vol`) is a recognizable word.\n\n**Duplicate emoji.** Both `system` and `display` categories use the same desktop emoji in the help listing (bin/mac:51-52), making them visually indistinguishable at a glance.\n\n**Hidden command.** `system detailed-info` exists in the dispatcher (system.sh:504-506) but is not listed in `system_help()` and has no search entry. Users cannot discover it without reading source code.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Help System UX (82/100)\n\n### What Works\n\nThe help system is multi-layered and well-structured:\n\n1. **`mac` or `mac help`** -- Shows the main help with all categories, usage syntax, examples, and global shortcuts.\n2. **`mac help <category>`** -- Shows category-specific help with command table, examples, tips, and shortcuts.\n3. **`mac <category> help`** -- Same result, accessible from within a category.\n4. **`-h` / `--help`** -- Accepted everywhere, following POSIX conventions.\n5. **`mac search <term>`** -- Full-text search across all modules.\n\nEvery help page includes:\n- A formatted command table with descriptions\n- Concrete usage examples with comments\n- Tips section with practical advice\n- Global shortcut references where applicable\n\nThe error messages for unknown commands always suggest using `mac help <category>` (e.g., finder.sh:306-308), creating a clear path from confusion to clarity. This is excellent UX.\n\n### What Needs Improvement\n\n**Search quality.** The search implementation in every module's `_search()` function uses hardcoded string matching: `[[ \"wifi\" == *\"$search_term\"* ]]`. This has several failure modes:\n- `mac search \"kill port\"` will not match `kill-port` (space vs. hyphen)\n- `mac search \"wifi connect\"` searches each module independently, so it matches `wifi` in the wifi module but misses the `connect` action context\n- Searching for a category name like `mac search \"audio\"` returns audio module results but does not highlight that `mac vol` is a shortcut\n- The search functions are manually maintained and will drift from the actual command set as new commands are added\n\nA better approach would be to extract the search corpus from the dispatcher's case statements or help text, and split search terms on spaces and hyphens.\n\n**No extended documentation.** The help text is concise by design (good for discovery) but there is no mechanism for deeper documentation. Adding `--verbose` to help could show exit codes, environment variables (like `SUPERMAC_DEBUG`), related commands, and troubleshooting guidance.\n\n**Category listing in version output.** `mac version` (bin/mac:153) lists categories as a flat string but does not show a count, making it hard to gauge the tool's scope at a glance.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Error Messages (75/100)\n\n### What Works\n\nError messages are consistently formatted and actionable. Every error follows the pattern: state what went wrong, then suggest how to fix it.\n\nExamples of good error messages:\n- `finder.sh:304-308`: \"Unknown finder action: X\" followed by \"Available actions: restart, show-hidden, hide-hidden, toggle-hidden, reveal, status\" and \"Use 'mac help finder' for detailed information\"\n- `dev.sh:201-204`: \"Port 8000 is already in use\" followed by \"Use 'mac dev kill-port 8000' to free it\"\n- `audio.sh:217-220`: \"Device name required\" followed by \"Usage: mac audio output <device_name>\" and \"Use 'mac audio devices' to see available devices\"\n\nThe `print_error()` function in utils.sh:94-96 redirects to stderr (`>&2`), which is correct -- error messages should not pollute stdout when output is piped.\n\n### What Needs Improvement\n\n**sudo operations have poor error messaging.** Commands like `network_flush_dns()` (network.sh:199-216) run `sudo dscacheutil -flushcache` and `sudo killall -HUP mDNSResponder` without pre-checking sudo access. If the user is non-admin or sudo requires a password in a non-interactive context, the error message will be the raw sudo output, not a SuperMac-formatted message. A pre-flight check like `sudo -n true 2>/dev/null || { print_warning \"This command requires admin privileges\"; ... }` would be more helpful.\n\n**set -euo pipefail gaps.** The main dispatcher sets strict mode (bin/mac:18) but the library modules do not. The `set -u` (undefined variable) protection is particularly important -- without it, a typo in a variable name inside a module function will silently expand to an empty string rather than failing fast. The dead `setup_error_handling()` function in utils.sh:460-463 suggests this was considered but never integrated.\n\n**Silent failures in piped while loops.** Many commands pipe data into `while read` loops (e.g., system.sh:74 `df -h / | tail -1 | while read ...`). Because the while loop runs in a subshell, any errors inside it are silently swallowed. The `set -e` from the parent does not propagate into subshells created by pipes.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Output Formatting (80/100)\n\n### What Works\n\nThe output system is visually cohesive and well-engineered:\n\n- **Consistent visual language**: checkmark for success, X for errors, info icon, warning triangle for warnings\n- **Unicode box drawing** (utils.sh:53-71) gives help pages a polished, structured look\n- **Non-TTY fallback** (utils.sh:73-83) automatically degrades to ASCII (+, -, |) when output is piped\n- **Layered formatting functions**: `print_header`, `print_subheader`, `print_command`, `print_dim` provide visual hierarchy\n- **Progress bar utility** (utils.sh:188-206) is available for long-running operations\n- **Contextual tips** follow almost every successful command, teaching users while they work\n\nThe formatting is not just decorative -- it serves information hierarchy. Values are highlighted with `print_command()` (cyan), metadata with `print_dim()`, and section headers with `print_header()`.\n\n### What Needs Improvement\n\n**Fixed-width layouts.** Help tables use hardcoded column widths (20 chars for command name, 35-40 for description) and fixed box widths (65-80 chars). On terminals narrower than the box width, alignment breaks. On wide terminals, the boxes look cramped with wasted space. Querying `tput cols` and adapting would improve the experience.\n\n**Version constant duplication.** `SUPERMAC_VERSION=\"2.1.0\"` is defined in both `bin/mac:43` and `lib/utils.sh:14`. This is a maintenance trap -- the next version bump will inevitably update one but not the other.\n\n**Fragile string construction.** `dock.sh:131` builds a success message by concatenating `$action` with `d!` outside of quotes: `print_success \"Dock auto-hide $action\"d!`. This works in bash but is confusing and fragile. Using `\"${action}d!\"` inside the quotes would be clearer.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Progressive Disclosure (77/100)\n\n### What Works\n\nThe tool does a good job of starting simple and revealing complexity:\n\n- **Level 1**: `mac` -- Shows categories and global shortcuts. A new user can immediately understand the tool's scope.\n- **Level 2**: `mac help finder` -- Shows all commands for a category with examples and tips.\n- **Level 3**: `mac finder reveal ~/secret` -- Executes a specific command with arguments.\n- **Level 4**: `mac debug system info` -- Enables verbose debug output for troubleshooting.\n\nThe global shortcuts serve as \"Level 0\" -- the most common operations don't even require knowing the category system. `mac ip`, `mac dark`, `mac cleanup` work immediately.\n\nThe tip system (e.g., \"Low brightness - good for nighttime use\") teaches users about related commands and features during normal use, gradually expanding their knowledge without requiring them to read documentation.\n\n### What Needs Improvement\n\n**No --dry-run mode.** Destructive commands like `system cleanup` and `network reset` have no way to preview what they would do without actually doing it. A `--dry-run` flag that lists files to be deleted or settings to be changed would significantly improve user confidence.\n\n**Missing --quiet mode.** Every command outputs multiple lines of context (info messages, success messages, tips). In scripted contexts, this is noisy. A `--quiet` flag that outputs only the essential result (e.g., just the IP address from `mac network ip`) would make the tool useful in shell scripts and CI pipelines.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Discoverability (70/100)\n\n### What Works\n\n- Running `mac` with no arguments shows the main help -- this is the gold standard for CLI discoverability.\n- Unknown commands suggest alternatives: \"Available actions: ...\" followed by \"Use 'mac help <category>' for detailed information.\"\n- Every category help page shows examples with inline comments.\n- The search function (`mac search <term>`) provides cross-module search.\n\n### What Needs Improvement\n\n**Search is weak.** As detailed in the findings, the hardcoded search functions miss multi-word queries, hyphenated variants, and typos. A user searching for \"disk\" will find `system disk-usage`, but a user searching for \"storage\" will also find it (because \"storage\" is in the search function's if-condition), while a user searching for \"space\" will not find anything. The search quality depends entirely on which keywords the developer remembered to include in the `_search()` function.\n\n**Undocumented aliases and hidden commands.** `system detailed-info`, `wifi enable/disable`, dock single-letter shortcuts -- all invisible to the user.\n\n**No autocomplete.** There is no bash/zsh completion script provided. For a tool with 85+ commands across 9 categories, tab completion would significantly improve discoverability and reduce typos.\n\n**No `mac list` or `mac commands` overview.** The only way to see all commands is to run `mac help` for each category individually. A `mac list` command that outputs every command in a flat list would help users who know what they want to do but don't know which category it's in.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Interactive Prompts (73/100)\n\n### What Works\n\nThe `confirm()` function (utils.sh:284-312) is well-designed:\n- Shows `[Y/n]` or `[y/N]` based on the default\n- Accepts yes/no in any case\n- Falls back to the default on empty input\n- Recursively re-prompts on invalid input with a helpful message\n\nIt is used appropriately in destructive contexts: `system_cleanup`, `network_reset`, `dock_reset`, `screenshot_reset`, and `dev_localhost` (when no service is detected on the port).\n\nThe `prompt_input()` function (utils.sh:315-347) supports optional validation and default values.\n\n### What Needs Improvement\n\n**No --yes flag.** There is no way to bypass interactive prompts for scripted use. Running `mac system cleanup` in a CI script will hang waiting for user input. A `--yes` or `-y` global flag that auto-confirms all prompts would solve this.\n\n**No --no-input flag.** Similarly, there is no flag to fail immediately when a command would require input, which is useful in CI to detect that a command is interactive.\n\n**confirm() does not work in non-interactive shells.** The `read -r response` (utils.sh:295) will fail silently in a non-interactive shell (stdin is /dev/null), causing the function to recurse indefinitely or hang. A check for `[[ -t 0 ]]` at the start of `confirm()` would allow graceful failure.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Accessibility (52/100)\n\nThis is the weakest area of the tool and the primary drag on the overall score.\n\n### Issues\n\n1. **No NO_COLOR support.** The industry-standard `NO_COLOR` environment variable (endorsed by no-color.org and supported by hundreds of CLI tools) is not respected. There is also no `--no-color` command-line flag. Device switching requires SwitchAudioSource (brew). Volume uses percentage like brightness.\"\n    },\n    \"screenshot\": {\n      \"count\": 10,\n      \"commands\": [\"location\", \"format\", \"shadows\", \"show-cursor\", \"thumbnail\", \"sound\", \"name-format\", \"take\", \"reset\", \"status\"],\n      \"quality_notes\": \"Most comprehensive settings module. Clipboard mode is well-handled. take sub-command offers screen/area/window modes.\"\n    },\n    \"global_shortcuts\": {\n      \"count\": 7,\n      \"commands\": [\"ip\", \"cleanup\", \"restart-finder\", \"kp\", \"vol\", \"dark\", \"light\"],\n      \"quality_notes\": \"Well-chosen for frequency of use. 'kp' is memorable for kill-port. No conflicts detected with standard macOS commands.\"\n    },\n    \"total_commands\": 73,\n    \"total_with_global\": 80\n  }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n# SuperMac v2.1.0 -- UX & CLI Design Audit Report\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nSuperMac scores **72/100** for overall UX and CLI design quality. It demonstrates strong architectural consistency across its 9 modules and 73+ commands, with a clean two-tier dispatch pattern, thorough help coverage, and thoughtful error messages. The primary weaknesses are in **accessibility** (55/100) -- the tool lacks NO_COLOR support, relies on emoji for semantic meaning, and provides no way to bypass interactive prompts. **Command design** (78/100) is generally strong but undermined by inconsistent boolean parsing, hidden commands, and duplicate constants.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Command Design (78/100)\n\nSuperMac uses a `mac <category> <action> [args]` pattern. This is a well-established CLI convention (used by `git`, `docker`, `npm`, `brew`) and is a good choice for a tool with 73+ commands.\n\n**What works well:**\n\nThe category names are intuitive and map cleanly to their domains: `finder`, `wifi`, `network`, `system`, `dev`, `display`, `dock`, `audio`, `screenshot`. Action names use kebab-case consistently (`show-hidden`, `dark-mode`, `kill-port`, `disk-usage`), which is the correct convention for multi-word CLI subcommands.\n\nThe global shortcuts system is the best design decision in the entire tool. Commands like `mac ip`, `mac dark`, `mac cleanup`, `mac kp 3000`, and `mac vol 50` eliminate the two-tier nesting for the most frequent operations. These are well-chosen: they are short, memorable, and do not conflict with any standard macOS commands.\n\nThe `mac` entry point handles both `mac help <category>` and `mac <category> help` implicitly via each module's dispatcher accepting `\"help\"|\"-h\"|\"--help\"`. Combined with `mac -h` and `mac --help`, there are effectively four ways to reach help -- excellent for discoverability.\n\n**Problems identified:**\n\nBoolean argument handling is inconsistent across modules. The dock module (`dock.sh:98-100`) accepts 8 synonyms for on/off (`on/off/enable/disable/true/false/1/0`), while wifi accepts only 2 (`on/enable`, `off/disable`), and screenshot accepts 4 (`on/off/enable/disable`). This is a maintenance burden and confuses users who expect consistent behavior. A shared `parse_boolean()` function in utils.sh would solve this cleanly.\n\nThe `system` module exposes a `detailed-info` action (`system.sh:504-506`) that is not listed in the help output (`system.sh:419-449`). This is a discoverability violation. Either document it or merge it into `info` with a `--verbose` flag.\n\nThe `SUPERMAC_VERSION` constant is defined in two places (`bin/mac:43` and `lib/utils.sh:14`). This is a maintenance trap. The version should be defined once in utils.sh (which is always loaded first) and removed from bin/mac.\n\nThe `display resolution` command requires an explicit `list` sub-action but does not provide a sensible default. Running `mac display resolution` without arguments gives an error. Compare with `mac network locations` which defaults to `list` when no sub-action is provided (`network.sh:339`). The display module should follow the same pattern.\n\nUndocumented aliases create an invisible feature layer. Commands like `mac wifi on` also accept `enable`, `mac dock position left` also accepts `l`, and `mac system memory` also accepts `mem` -- but none of these appear in help output. Users who discover one alias will expect others that may not exist.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Help System UX (82/100)\n\nThis is the strongest category. The help system is thorough, consistent, and multi-layered.\n\n**Architecture:**\n\nEvery module implements three help-related functions: `<module>_help()` for detailed help, `<module>_search()` for keyword search, and `<module>_dispatch()` which handles `help/-h/--help`. The main dispatcher in `bin/mac` adds a top-level `show_main_help()`, `show_category_help()`, and `show_version()`. This is a well-structured approach.\n\nRunning `mac` with no arguments shows the main help, which is the correct behavior. The main help includes: usage syntax, category listing with emoji+descriptions, quick commands, examples, and global shortcuts. This is more comprehensive than many similar tools.\n\nEach module's help includes: a formatted command table, usage examples, tips, and shortcuts. The `dev` module's help (`dev.sh:467-504`) is exemplary -- it includes a \"Development Workflow\" section that contextualizes commands for real-world use.\n\nThe search system (`bin/mac:159-192`) loads each module and calls its `_search()` function. This is a smart design that keeps search indexes close to the commands they describe.\n\n**Weaknesses:**\n\nThe search implementation uses fragile substring matching. Each module's `_search()` function is a hand-coded if/elif chain that checks specific keywords against the search term. For example, `wifi_search()` (`wifi.sh:430-456`) checks for exact substring matches against \"wifi\", \"wireless\", \"network\", \"connect\", etc. This misses synonyms (e.g., \"internet\" returns nothing from wifi), fails for partial matches (\"net\" does not match \"network\" because it checks `\"network\" == *\"net\"*` which works, but \"connect\" won't find the wifi connect command unless you type \"connect\"). The search would be more robust if it searched against the command names and descriptions that already exist in the help tables.\n\nThe box-drawing widths vary across modules (65, 70, 75, 80 characters). This is a visual inconsistency that suggests the modules were developed independently without a shared width constant.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Error Messages (80/100)\n\nError messages are a genuine strength of this tool. Nearly every error follows a three-part pattern: what happened, why it might have happened, and what to do next.\n\n**Pattern analysis across modules:**\n\nThe canonical error format is:\n```\nprint_error \"Descriptive error\"\nprint_info \"Usage: mac <category> <action> [args]\"\nprint_info \"Use 'mac help <category>' for detailed information\"\n```\n\nThis pattern appears in all 9 module dispatchers for unknown actions, and in argument validation throughout. Examples:\n\n- `finder.sh:304-308`: Unknown action lists all available actions and points to help.\n- `wifi.sh:311-314`: Missing network name provides usage syntax.\n- `audio.sh:217-219`: Missing device name tells user to run `mac audio devices` to see options.\n- `dev.sh:34-36`: Missing port provides usage and the error explains the argument type.\n- `network.sh:228-229`: Missing host provides usage with the optional count argument.\n\nThe error messages also differentiate between validation failures (bad input) and operational failures (something went wrong). For example, `dev_kill_port()` (`dev.sh:38-65`) validates the port is a number (line 39-41) separately from checking if anything is listening on it (line 63).\n\n**Weaknesses:**\n\nThe `confirm()` function (`utils.sh:308`) prints \"Please answer yes or no.\" and recursively calls itself on invalid input. This is technically infinite recursion with no escape -- a user can get stuck in a loop by repeatedly entering invalid input. A retry counter would be safer.\n\nSome error messages use ambiguous phrasing. `dock.sh:131`: `\"Dock auto-hide $actiond!\"` has a grammatical error -- when action is \"enable\", it prints \"enable\" + \"d!\" = \"enabled!\" (correct), but when action is \"disable\", it prints \"disabled!\" (also correct). This works but is fragile string concatenation.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Output Formatting (75/100)\n\nThe output system is built on a layered abstraction in `utils.sh` with print_success, print_error, print_info, print_warning, print_header, print_subheader, and print_command functions. Higher-level functions like print_banner, print_box, and print_progress provide structural formatting.\n\n**Color system:**\n\nColors are gated on `[[ -t 1 ]]` (utils.sh:24), which correctly detects non-TTY output (pipes, redirects). When stdout is not a TTY, all color variables are set to empty strings and box-drawing falls back to ASCII (`+`, `-`, `|`). This is correct behavior.\n\nHowever, the tool does not respect the `NO_COLOR` environment variable, which is an emerging standard supported by many CLI tools. This is a significant accessibility gap.\n\n**Visual consistency:**\n\nThe output uses a consistent visual hierarchy: headers are bold+blue, subheaders are bold, commands are cyan, dim text is gray, success is green, errors are red, warnings are yellow. This hierarchy is maintained across all modules.\n\nThe box-drawing system creates visually appealing help displays. However, the `print_category_header()` function (`utils.sh:546-558`) calculates string widths using `${#variable}`, which does not account for emoji display width. The emoji 📁 may be 1 character in bash string length but renders as 2 terminal columns, causing the right border to be offset by 1-2 characters.\n\nThe progress bar function (`utils.sh:188-206`) uses Unicode block characters (full block and light shade) which are attractive but will render as empty boxes on terminals without Unicode support.\n\n**Tip messages:**\n\nEvery successful operation prints 1-3 contextual tips. For example, `finder_show_hidden()` prints two tips after success (`finder.sh:87-88`). These are helpful for new users but add significant noise for experienced users and are problematic in scripted usage. There is no way to suppress them.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Progressive Disclosure (analysis)\n\nThe tool does a reasonable job of progressive disclosure:\n\n- **Level 1**: `mac` -- shows categories, shortcuts, and examples.\n- **Level 2**: `mac help <category>` -- shows all actions in that category with examples and tips.\n- **Level 3**: Module dispatchers accept `-h`/`--help` as well.\n- **Level 4**: `mac search <term>` -- keyword search across all modules.\n- **Level 5**: `mac --debug` -- verbose debug output for troubleshooting.\n\nThe `--debug` flag is available as both `mac debug ...` (subcommand) and `mac --debug ...` (flag), which is redundant. Both do the same thing: set `SUPERMAC_DEBUG=1` and re-invoke `main()`. The dual entry point adds confusion without adding value.\n\nWhat is missing is a middle ground between normal output and debug mode. There is no `--quiet` flag for suppressing tips and informational messages, and no `--verbose` flag for getting more detail without full debug spew. This means users have three modes: normal (chatty), debug (everything), or they pipe to /dev/null.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Discoverability (72/100)\n\nDiscoverability is good but has notable gaps.\n\n**What works:**\n\nRunning `mac` with no arguments shows help -- the most important discoverability feature. The help output is comprehensive, listing all categories with emoji and descriptions, showing examples, and highlighting global shortcuts. The search function (`mac search <term>`) provides a way to find commands without knowing the category.\n\nEvery module's unknown-action handler lists available actions (e.g., `wifi.sh:500`: \"Available actions: on, off, toggle, status, info, scan, connect, forget, list-saved\"). This means typos like `mac wifi tooogle` produce a helpful error with the correct options.\n\n**What does not work:**\n\nThe search function relies on hardcoded keyword lists in each module's `_search()` function. This means:\n- Searching for \"internet\" returns nothing (wifi_search checks \"wifi\" and \"wireless\" but not \"internet\").\n- Searching for \"theme\" returns nothing (display_search checks \"dark\", \"mode\", and \"theme\" -- actually it does, but other modules do not check synonyms consistently).\n- Searching for \"bluetooth\" returns nothing because there is no bluetooth module, but the error message does not suggest this.\n- The search results lack context about which category a command belongs to (the wrapper adds category headers, but the results themselves are plain command listings).\n\nThere is no `mac list` or `mac commands` command that shows all 73 commands in a flat list. Users must browse category by category. For a tool with this many commands, a comprehensive listing would be valuable.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Interactive Prompts\n\nThe `confirm()` function (`utils.sh:284-311`) is used by four destructive operations: system cleanup, dock reset, network reset, and screenshot reset. It correctly defaults to \"no\" for destructive operations and \"yes\" for routine ones (system cleanup defaults to Y, which is debatable for a command that deletes files).\n\n**Critical limitation:** There is no `--yes` or `--force` flag to bypass confirmation prompts. This makes the tool impossible to use non-interactively in scripts, CI pipelines, or automation. The `confirm()` function always reads from stdin. A global `SUPERMAC_YES` environment variable or `--yes` flag would solve this.\n\nThe `prompt_input()` function (`utils.sh:315-347`) exists in utils.sh and supports validation functions and default values, but is never actually used by any module. It appears to be infrastructure that was built but not adopted.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Accessibility (55/100)\n\nThis is the weakest category and the primary drag on the overall score.\n\n**Color-only information:**\n\nThe `dev_cpu_hogs()` function (`dev.sh:277-293`) uses red color for high CPU usage and yellow for moderate. There is no textual indicator. A colorblind user or a user on a monochrome terminal sees no differentiation.\n\n**Emoji dependency:**\n\nThe help system, status commands, and output messages rely on emoji for both decoration and semantic meaning. The emoji in the CATEGORIES associative array (`bin/mac:47-57`) serve as visual identifiers. While visually appealing, they add zero information value for screen reader users and may render as empty boxes on some terminals.\n\n**NO_COLOR spec:**\n\nThe tool does not respect the `NO_COLOR` environment variable (https://no-color.org/), which is supported by an increasing number of CLI tools. Adding support would be a single line change: `if [[ -t 1 ]] && [[ -z \"${NO_COLOR:-}\" ]]; then`.\n\n**Unicode box drawing:**\n\nThe fallback from Unicode box drawing to ASCII only triggers when stdout is not a TTY. Many terminal environments (especially over SSH to older systems) are TTYs that do not support Unicode. The tool should detect Unicode capability separately from color capability.\n\n---\n\n## 9. Global Shortcuts\n\nThe 7 global shortcuts are well-chosen:\n\n| Shortcut | Maps To | Frequency Rationale |\n|----------|---------|-------------------|\n| `ip` | `network:ip` | Extremely common lookup |\n| `cleanup` | `system:cleanup` | Weekly maintenance task |\n| `restart-finder` | `finder:restart` | Common troubleshooting |\n| `kp` | `dev:kill-port` | Frequent during development |\n| `vol` | `audio:volume` | Daily adjustment |\n| `dark` | `display:dark-mode` | Preference toggle |\n| `light` | `display:light-mode` | Preference toggle |\n\n`kp` is particularly well-designed -- it is short, memorable, and does not conflict with any standard command. `ip` is aggressive (shadows the hostname command on some systems) but is justified by frequency of use.\n\nNo conflicts were detected with standard macOS commands or common CLI tools.\n\n---\n\n## 10. Exit Codes (analysis)\n\nThe tool uses exit codes correctly and consistently:\n\n- `return 0` for success (all modules).\n- `return 1` for errors (all modules).\n- `exit 1` only in the main dispatcher for fatal errors (missing utils.sh).\n- The `die()` function (`utils.sh:448-451`) supports custom exit codes via a second argument.\n\nThe `set -euo pipefail` in `bin/mac:18` ensures that unset variables, failed commands, and pipe failures all cause the script to exit with non-zero status.\n\nOne concern: the subshell patterns used extensively (e.g., `ps aux | sort | head | while read ...`) mean that `return` inside the while loop exits the subshell, not the function. If a command inside a piped while-loop fails, the error is not propagated to the caller. This is a fundamental limitation of the Bash piped-while pattern and affects functions like `system_processes()` and `dev_list_ports()`.\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Recommendations by Priority\n\n**Must fix (CRITICAL/HIGH):**\n1. Add `NO_COLOR` environment variable support and `--no-color` flag.\n2. Add textual fallbacks for emoji-only status indicators.\n3. Create a shared `parse_boolean()` function and use it consistently.\n4. Remove the duplicate `SUPERMAC_VERSION` constant from bin/mac.\n5. Add textual severity indicators alongside color in process listings.\n6. Separate Unicode capability detection from color detection.\n\n**Should fix (MEDIUM):**\n7. Add `--yes` flag to bypass interactive confirmation prompts.\n8. Define a constant `HELP_WIDTH` for consistent box widths.\n9. Replace hardcoded search indexes with a centralized command registry.\n10. Add `--quiet` and `--verbose` flags as gradations between normal and debug output.\n11. Document or remove the hidden `detailed-info` command.\n12. Consolidate the duplicate `debug`/`--debug` entry points.\n\n**Nice to have (LOW):**\n13. Document command aliases in help output.\n14. Make `mac display resolution` default to `list`.\n15. Add retry limits to the `confirm()` function.\n16. Provide ASCII fallbacks for progress bar characters.\n\n---\n\n**Files analyzed:**\n- `/Users/gab/PROJECTS/SuperMac/bin/mac` (349 lines) -- main dispatcher\n- `/Users/gab/PROJECTS/SuperMac/lib/utils.sh` (589 lines) -- shared utilities\n- `/Users/gab/PROJECTS/SuperMac/lib/finder.sh` (313 lines)\n- `/Users/gab/PROJECTS/SuperMac/lib/wifi.sh` (507 lines)\n- `/Users/gab/PROJECTS/SuperMac/lib/network.sh` (484 lines)\n- `/Users/gab/PROJECTS/SuperMac/lib/system.sh` (541 lines)\n- `/Users/gab/PROJECTS/SuperMac/lib/dev.sh` (610 lines)\n- `/Users/gab/PROJECTS/SuperMac/lib/display.sh` (428 lines)\n- `/Users/gab/PROJECTS/SuperMac/lib/dock.sh` (573 lines)\n- `/Users/gab/PROJECTS/SuperMac/lib/audio.sh` (519 lines)\n- `/Users/gab/PROJECTS/SuperMac/lib/screenshot.sh` (590 lines)\n\n**Total analyzed: 5,503 lines of Bash across 11 files.**"}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":37,"cache_creation_input_tokens":0,"cache_read_input_tokens":72896,"output_tokens":8113,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"type":"assistant","uuid":"1b819b25-ef98-4e66-84d3-b7c38e24640c","timestamp":"2026-04-07T13:22:43.890Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/gab/PROJECTS/SuperMac","sessionId":"ee896f3b-ba3e-493e-ab51-73d0ef866e89","version":"2.1.92","gitBranch":"main","slug":"binary-sauteeing-dragonfly"}
